It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly.\n\n\"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding.\n\n\"But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies.\n\n\"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix.\n\n\"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nStewart-Haas Racing has four Cup teams and two Xfinity teams. SHR fields cars in Cup for Chase Briscoe, Ryan Preece, Noah Gragson and Josh Berry. SHR fields Xfinity cars for reigning series champion Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nHaas started the team in 2002 but it wasn't 2003 that the team ran a full Cup season with a variety of drivers.\n\nHaas and Tony Stewart announced in July 2018 that they would form Stewart-Haas Racing beginning with the 2009 season. Stewart left Joe Gibbs Racing to join SHR in 2009. The organization ran two cars from 2009-12 (Stewart and Ryan Newman were the drivers) before expanding to a third car in 2013, adding Danica Patrick.\n\nSHR became a four-car team in 2014 with a lineup of Stewart, Kurt Busch, Kevin Harvick and Patrick.\n\nIt was granted four charters in 2016 when NASCAR and team owners created the system.\n\nStewart won the 2011 Cup title and Harvick won the 2014 crown with the organization, but it has not had a driver finish in the top 10 in points in the past two seasons.\n\nSHR's most recent victory came in August 2022 by Harvick at Richmond. Eleven other Cup organizations have won since that race.\n\nSHR switched from Chevrolet to Ford for the 2017 season and had been a Ford team since. {"uri": "2024-05-371340392", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "21:24:02", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T21:24:02Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T21:13:32Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8549019694328308, "url": "https://www.wtaj.com/sports/ap-sports/ap-stewart-haas-racing-to-close-nascar-teams-at-end-of-2024-season-says-time-to-pass-the-torch/", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to close NASCAR teams at end of 2024 season, says time to 'pass the torch'", "body": "CHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Stewart-Haas Racing, a two-time NASCAR championship team with 69 Cup Series victories since its 2009 formation, will close its organization at the end of this season\n\nCo-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced the decision after nearly a year of rumors that their four-car Cup team was looking to sell its charters and either scale back or exit the stock car series completely. The news was delivered to the nearly 300 SHR employees late Tuesday afternoon.\n\n\"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly,\" the owners said. \"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nSHR this year fields Cup cars for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. Berry and Gragson are in their first seasons with the team. SHR holds the 2025 option on Briscoe and he has not been permitted to discuss future employment options even as rumors have swirled that SHR would close.\n\n\"Stewart Haas has been home to my family and I for the last 7 years and at the end of the year myself and the entire organization will be looking for a new home and new opportunities in the Cup series,\" Briscoe posted on social media. \"I have amazing partners behind me and can't wait to get them back in victory lane.\"\n\nThe move will also shutter the SHR Xfinity Series team, whose two cars are driven by Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nGene Haas founded Haas CNC Racing in 2002 and the California businessman lured Stewart in as a co-owner ahead of the 2009 season. Stewart had won two Cup championships for Joe Gibbs Racing at the time but couldn't turn down an equity stake and opportunity to help a small team contend for titles.\n\nStewart in his 2009 debut season gave the rebranded team its first Cup victory -- he won four races that year -- and its first Cup title in 2011. Kevin Harvick added a second championship in 2014.\n\nStewart, Harvick and Clint Bowyer have all retired from NASCAR driving and SHR since then has been in a grueling rebuild. The organization's last Cup Series win was in 2022 with Harvick a year before he retired. SHR didn't win a Cup race last season.\n\nThe team also is set to lose some of its support from Ford at the end of the season, although Mark Rushbrook, the global director of Ford Performance, told The Associated Press last week he had no idea what SHR's plans are beyond this year.\n\nSHR also lost major sponsorship this season when Smithfield Foods exited NASCAR and Anheuser-Busch moved to Trackhouse Racing.\n\nHaas spends most of his time with his Formula 1 team and Stewart is driving a full NHRA schedule, making both absentee owners at NASCAR events. The 71-year-old Haas was also ill for much of last year.\n\nThe NASCAR team is primarily run by Joe Custer, the chief operating officer and longtime Gene Haas confidant. His son, Cole, won the Xfinity championship last year for SHR.\n\nAmong SHR's accomplishments are the two Cup titles, two Xfinity championships and victories that include crown-jewel events such as the Daytona 500, Brickyard 400 and Southern 500.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said. \"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nPart of Haas' F1 team is run from the Kannapolis-based shop and it is unclear if that will continue or if Haas has plans to also depart from F1.\n\nIt's also not clear what happens to the four charters SHR holds that guarantee entry into the field every week. Spire Motorsports last year bought a charter for $40 million, but the actual charter value fluctuates annually.\n\nTeams are in a bitter fight with NASCAR over charters, which are set to expire at the end of this season. The teams want them made permanent and not renewable but NASCAR has refused to budge on the issue.\n\nShould SHR be able to sell the charters, it appears there is interest from Front Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing and Trackhouse. There is also speculation that Joe Custer may retain one of the charters and run a car for his son.\n\nWhere SHR's drivers land is unknown. Briscoe should be able to start talking to other teams now about his future. The team also held an option for next year on Berry, who doesn't bring much personal sponsorship and got the break of his career when SHR hired him ahead of this season.\n\nGragson's contract was announced as a multi-year deal and has backing from Bass Pro Shops to take to another team. Preece is in a contract year with SHR so was already free to shop around the series.\n\nCole Custer could end up in a car in either Cup or the Xfinity Series with backing of Haas' CNC Automation company, wile Herbst has significant financial backing from Monster Energy that should give him options.", "source": {"uri": "wtaj.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "WTAJ - www.wtaj.com"}, "authors": {"uri": "8150537100", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "21:37:32", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T21:37:32Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T21:37:01Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8549019694328308, "url": "https://journalnow.com/news/state/stewart-haas-racing-to-close-nascar-teams-at-end-of-2024-season-says-time-to/article_fc87d838-1d56-52d8-a429-f668353e3742.html", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to close NASCAR teams at end of 2024 season, says time to 'pass the torch'", "body": "By JENNA FRYER - AP Auto Racing Writer\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Stewart-Haas Racing, a two-time NASCAR championship team with 69 Cup Series victories since its 2009 formation, will close its organization at the end of this season\n\nCo-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced the decision after nearly a year of rumors that their four-car Cup team was looking to sell its charters and either scale back or exit the stock car series completely. The news was delivered to the nearly 300 SHR employees late Tuesday afternoon.\n\n\"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly,\" the owners said. \"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nSHR this year fields Cup cars for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. Berry and Gragson are in their first seasons with the team. SHR holds the 2025 option on Briscoe and he has not been permitted to discuss future employment options even as rumors have swirled that SHR would close.\n\n\"Stewart Haas has been home to my family and I for the last 7 years and at the end of the year myself and the entire organization will be looking for a new home and new opportunities in the Cup series,\" Briscoe posted on social media. \"I have amazing partners behind me and can't wait to get them back in victory lane.\"\n\nThe move will also shutter the SHR Xfinity Series team, whose two cars are driven by Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nGene Haas founded Haas CNC Racing in 2002 and the California businessman lured Stewart in as a co-owner ahead of the 2009 season. Stewart had won two Cup championships for Joe Gibbs Racing at the time but couldn't turn down an equity stake and opportunity to help a small team contend for titles.\n\nStewart in his 2009 debut season gave the rebranded team its first Cup victory -- he won four races that year -- and its first Cup title in 2011. Kevin Harvick added a second championship in 2014.\n\nStewart, Harvick and Clint Bowyer have all retired from NASCAR driving and SHR since then has been in a grueling rebuild. The organization's last Cup Series win was in 2022 with Harvick a year before he retired. SHR didn't win a Cup race last season.\n\nThe team also is set to lose some of its support from Ford at the end of the season, although Mark Rushbrook, the global director of Ford Performance, told The Associated Press last week he had no idea what SHR's plans are beyond this year.\n\nSHR also lost major sponsorship this season when Smithfield Foods exited NASCAR and Anheuser-Busch moved to Trackhouse Racing.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack | All Of Our Podcasts\n\nHaas spends most of his time with his Formula 1 team and Stewart is driving a full NHRA schedule, making both absentee owners at NASCAR events. The 71-year-old Haas was also ill for much of last year.\n\nThe NASCAR team is primarily run by Joe Custer, the chief operating officer and longtime Gene Haas confidant. His son, Cole, won the Xfinity championship last year for SHR.\n\nAmong SHR's accomplishments are the two Cup titles, two Xfinity championships and victories that include crown-jewel events such as the Daytona 500, Brickyard 400 and Southern 500.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said. \"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nPart of Haas' F1 team is run from the Kannapolis-based shop and it is unclear if that will continue or if Haas has plans to also depart from F1.\n\nIt's also not clear what happens to the four charters SHR holds that guarantee entry into the field every week. Spire Motorsports last year bought a charter for $40 million, but the actual charter value fluctuates annually.\n\nTeams are in a bitter fight with NASCAR over charters, which are set to expire at the end of this season. The teams want them made permanent and not renewable but NASCAR has refused to budge on the issue.\n\nShould SHR be able to sell the charters, it appears there is interest from Front Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing and Trackhouse. There is also speculation that Joe Custer may retain one of the charters and run a car for his son.\n\nWhere SHR's drivers land is unknown. Briscoe should be able to start talking to other teams now about his future. The team also held an option for next year on Berry, who doesn't bring much personal sponsorship and got the break of his career when SHR hired him ahead of this season.\n\nGragson's contract was announced as a multi-year deal and has backing from Bass Pro Shops to take to another team. Preece is in a contract year with SHR so was already free to shop around the series.\n\nCole Custer could end up in a car in either Cup or the Xfinity Series with backing of Haas' CNC Automation company, wile Herbst has significant financial backing from Monster Energy that should give him options.\n\nAP auto racing: https://apnews.com/hub/auto-racing\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. All rights reserved. Spire Motorsports last year bought a charter for $40 million, but the actual charter value fluctuates annually.\n\nTeams are in a bitter fight with NASCAR over charters, which are set to expire at the end of this season. The teams want them made permanent and not renewable but NASCAR has refused to budge on the issue.\n\nShould SHR be able to sell the charters, it appears there is interest from Front Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing and Trackhouse. There is also speculation that Joe Custer may retain one of the charters and run a car for his son.\n\nWhere SHR's drivers land is unknown. Briscoe should be able to start talking to other teams now about his future. The team also held an option for next year on Berry, who doesn't bring much personal sponsorship and got the break of his career when SHR hired him ahead of this season.\n\nGragson's contract was announced as a multi-year deal and has backing from Bass Pro Shops to take to another team. Preece is in a contract year with SHR so was already free to shop around the series.\n\nCole Custer could end up in a car in either Cup or the Xfinity Series with backing of Haas' CNC Automation {"uri": "2024-05-371321841", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "20:55:35", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T20:55:35Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T20:39:04Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8078431487083435, "url": "https://www.aol.com/nascar-stewart-haas-racing-shutting-203904817.html", "title": "NASCAR: Stewart-Haas Racing shutting down Cup Series team at end of 2024 season", "body": "NASCAR: Stewart-Haas Racing shutting down Cup Series team at end of 2024 season\n\nNick Bromberg\n\nMay 28, 2024 at 10:39 PM\n\nOne of NASCAR's biggest teams is ceasing its Cup Series operations.\n\nStewart-Haas Racing announced Tuesday that it is shutting down its top-level NASCAR team. The team, formed in 2009 when Tony Stewart became a co-owner with Gene Haas, currently fields four cars in the Cup Series for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. It also runs a two-car operation in the Xfinity Series for Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\n\"We have made the difficult decisions to close Stewart-Haas Racing at the conclusion of the 2024 season,\" a statement from Haas and Stewart said. \"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly.\"\n\n\"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding.\"\n\n\"But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed for a common cause -- winning races and collecting trophies.\"\n\n\"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix.\"\n\n\"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nSHR's closure comes as the team lost two longtime sponsors at the end of the 2023 season. Busch Light moved to Ross Chastain's No. 1 car at Trackhouse Racing following Kevin Harvick's retirement and Smithfield left NASCAR completely when Aric Almirola retired from full-time competition.\n\nStewart became the first driver-owner to win a NASCAR Cup Series title when he won his third championship driving for SHR in 2011. Three years later, Harvick won the Cup Series title.\n\nSince then, things have slowly trended downwards for the team even as Harvick was a stalwart. Harvick was 13th in the points standings a season ago while Almirola, Briscoe and Preece all finished outside the top 20. The organization went winless across an entire Cup Series season for the first time ever.\n\nRumors of a downsizing or total shuttering have been floated for months as SHR did not have a contract with Ford beyond the 2024 season. Teams typically have their manufacturers lined up years into the future.\n\nFour charters available\n\nThe closure of Stewart-Haas means that teams looking to expand may not have to pay top rate for a charter -- essentially NASCAR's version of a franchise. The 36 cars with charters are guaranteed entry into every single Cup Series race and also a bigger share of prize money.\n\nThe only charter on the market ahead of the 2024 season sold for approximately $40 million when Spire purchased Live Fast Racing's charter in September of 2023. With all four SHR charters now on the market, it'll be a surprise if any of the team's guaranteed entries sell for close to that number.\n\nTrackhouse could be in the market for another charter along with Front Row Motorsports. Trackhouse is loaning Zane Smith to Spire Motorsports in 2024 and an additional charter or two can make room at the two-car team for him and/or Shane van Gisbergen.\n\nThe charter agreement between NASCAR and teams currently limits teams to a maximum of four charters. However, that agreement expires at the end of the 2024 season and the sanctioning body and its teams don't seem close to terms on a new deal. In addition to SHR, Hendrick Motorsports and Joe Gibbs Racing also field four cars.", "source": {"uri": "aol.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Aol"}, "authors": [{"uri": "nick_bromberg@aol.com", {"uri": "8150576348", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "22:21:29", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T22:21:29Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T22:21:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.800000011920929, "url": "https://www.foxnews.com/sports/stewart-haas-racing-ceasing-cup-operations-after-2024-selling-four-charters", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing ceasing Cup operations after 2024, selling four charters", "body": "By entering your email and pushing continue, you are agreeing to Fox News' Terms of Use and Privacy Policy, which includes our Notice of Financial Incentive. To access the content, check your email and follow the instructions provided.\n\nStewart-Haas Racing, which has won two Cup titles and captured 69 wins since its formation in 2009, will close after the 2024 season, shuttering a four-car Cup operation.\n\nCo-owners Gene Haas and Tony Stewart have appeared focused on other aspects of their businesses in recent years. Haas has a Formula 1 team that has struggled and the three-time Cup champion Stewart started an NHRA drag-racing team a couple of years ago that his wife drove for last year and Stewart is driving for this year.\n\nSHR has struggled in recent years and its hefty support from Ford is set to end after this season. It also lost two major sponsors in Smithfield and Anheuser-Busch prior to this year, so without that Ford support continuing it would have been difficult to sustain a four-car operation.\n\n\"We have made the difficult decision to close Stewart-Haas Racing at the conclusion of the 2024 season,\" Stewart and Haas said in a joint statement. \"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly.\n\n\"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nThe organization has four charters that it can sell, and sources indicated at least three of them will go to existing Cup organizations -- one to Front Row Motorsports, one to 23XI Racing and one to Trackhouse Racing. All three of those organizations indicated they had no comment on any charter acquisitions today. Where the fourth charter goes is not clear.\n\nNot having SHR on the Cup grid will be eye-opening next season. SHR started with Haas operating Haas CNC Racing in 2002. Haas gave Stewart half the team in 2009 for him to come drive and help operate the organization. They won championships in 2011 with Stewart and 2014 with Kevin Harvick.\n\nThe organization has 69 Cup wins with the last coming in 2022 with Harvick, who retired after the 2023 season.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause -- winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said in their statement.\n\n\"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix. We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nThe closure leaves Cup drivers Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson, Josh Berry and Ryan Preece in transition, as well as Xfinity Series drivers Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nHere's a quick look at what could happen with those drivers:\n\nBriscoe, who is 16th in the Cup standings, is the driver most often mentioned as a possibility to drive for Wood Brothers Racing next year with Harrison Burton on the hot seat as he struggles for the third consecutive year. Briscoe was in an option year with SHR and can now start to have more extensive talks with other teams.\n\nBriscoe said he has no idea where he will drive next year.\n\n\"Crazy time,\" Briscoe said in a video on X, formerly known as Twitter. \"I never thought this day would come. ... I just hope all of the guys and gals at this place finds a great opportunity because each and every single person here deserves it.\"\n\nBerry, at 19th in the standings in his rookie season and who has surged over the last month, was under contract with SHR for next year but obviously is now looking for a ride. He doesn't have much personal sponsorship but now will be talking heavily to sponsors and teams. Whether he remains in Cup is still to be determined.\n\nGragson's impressive run in his first season at SHR as he sits 21st in the standings (he'd be 19th if not for a 35-point penalty earlier this year plus what appears to be support from Bass Pro Shops, potentially could give him Cup options either at Front Row Motorsports or other teams.\n\nPreece sits 28th in the standings (he'd be 22nd if not for a 35-point penalty earlier this year) was already looking for next year as his contract was up after this season. His future seems uncertain.\n\nCuster, the former Cup driver and defending Xfinity Series champion who is third in the Xfinity standings, will be driving a car next year but still to be determined whether it is Xfinity or Cup. SHR's Xfinity programs -- it not only fields two cars but also supplies cars to other Ford teams -- could be siphoned off into a new team. Also, if Haas wants to continue involvement in NASCAR, Custer would be the natural driver for his Haas Automation company to sponsor as it has sponsored Custer for several years and Custer's father, Joe, is an SHR executive who has worked on Haas motorsports programs for decades.\n\nHerbst, seventh in the Xfintiy standings, has sponsorship from Monster Energy, and that should give him options, potentially on the Cup side.\n\nFRM (which would have two seats available) and 23XI will be seeking drivers if they obtain charters and would need sponsorship as well for them, making them possible landing spots for Herbst.\n\nTrackhouse already has a logjam of drivers with Ross Chastain, Shane van Gisbergen and Zane Smith currently under contract and Daniel Suarez expecting to sign an extension soon. There is a possibility the new charter system could limit organizations to three charters, and if that happens, Trackhouse would have to form an alliance with another team, keep van Gisbergen in Xfinity next year or release one of its drivers.\n\nLegacy Motor Club, RFK Racing and JTG Daugherty Racing have all considered expansion but are not expected to be in play for any of the SHR charters. Berry and Gragson are in their first seasons with the team. SHR holds the 2025 option on Briscoe and he has not been permitted to discuss future employment options even as rumors have swirled that SHR would close.\n\n\"Stewart Haas has been home to my family and I for the last 7 years, and at the end of the year myself and the entire organization will be looking for a new home and new opportunities in the Cup series,\" Briscoe posted on social media. \"I have amazing partners behind me and can't wait to get them back in victory lane.\"\n\nThe move will also shutter the SHR Xfinity Series team, whose two cars are driven by Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nGene Haas founded Haas CNC Racing in 2002 and the California businessman lured Stewart in as a co-owner ahead of the 2009 season. Stewart had won two Cup championships for Joe Gibbs Racing at the time, but couldn't turn down an equity stake and opportunity to help a small team contend for titles.\n\nStewart in his 2009 debut season gave the rebranded team its first Cup victory -- he won four races that year -- and its first Cup title in 2011. Kevin Harvick added a second championship in 2014.\n\nStewart, Harvick and Clint Bowyer have all retired from NASCAR driving, and SHR since then has been in a grueling rebuild. The organization's last Cup Series win was in 2022 with Harvick a year before he retired. SHR didn't win a Cup race last season.\n\nThe team also is set to lose some of its support from Ford at the end of the season, although Mark Rushbrook, the global director of Ford Performance, told The Associated Press last week he had no idea what SHR's plans are beyond this year.\n\nSHR also lost major sponsorship this season when Smithfield Foods exited NASCAR and Anheuser-Busch moved to Trackhouse Racing.\n\nHaas spends most of his time with his Formula 1 team, and Stewart is driving a full NHRA schedule, making both absentee owners at NASCAR events. The 71-year-old Haas was also ill for much of last year.\n\nThe NASCAR team is primarily run by Joe Custer, the chief operating officer and longtime Gene Haas confidant. His son, Cole, won the Xfinity championship last year for SHR.\n\nAmong SHR's accomplishments are the two Cup titles, two Xfinity championships and victories that include crown-jewel events such as the Daytona 500, Brickyard 400 and Southern 500.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause -- winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said. \"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nPart of Haas' F1 team is run from the Kannapolis-based shop, and it is unclear if that will continue or if Haas has plans to also depart from F1.\n\nIt's also not clear what happens to the four charters SHR holds that guarantee entry into the field every week. Spire Motorsports last year bought a charter for $40 million, but the actual charter value fluctuates annually.\n\nTeams are in a bitter fight with NASCAR over charters, which are set to expire at the end of this season. The teams want them made permanent and not renewable but NASCAR has refused to budge on the issue.\n\nShould SHR be able to sell the charters, it appears there is interest from Front Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing and Trackhouse. There is also speculation that Joe Custer may retain one of the charters and run a car for his son.\n\nWhere SHR's drivers land is unknown. {"uri": "8150533934", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "21:33:33", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T21:33:33Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T21:32:56Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7921568751335144, "url": "https://pantagraph.com/news/state-and-regional/illinois/stewart-haas-racing-to-close-nascar-teams-at-end-of-2024-season-says-time-to/article_876984f1-4bb2-5ef2-ac24-ad383595d587.html", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to close NASCAR teams at end of 2024 season, says time to 'pass the torch'", "body": "By JENNA FRYER - AP Auto Racing Writer\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Stewart-Haas Racing, a two-time NASCAR championship team with 69 Cup Series victories since its 2009 formation, will close its organization at the end of this season\n\nCo-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced the decision after nearly a year of rumors that their four-car Cup team was looking to sell its charters and either scale back or exit the stock car series completely. The news was delivered to the nearly 300 SHR employees late Tuesday afternoon.\n\n\"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly,\" the owners said. \"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nPeople are also reading... McLean County house rendered a total loss following weekend crash 'Gustnado' prompts sirens in Bloomington-Normal Bloomington educator retires after more than 40 years: 'Everyone has a job because of a teacher' Storms, blowing dust threaten Central Illinois Hudson man charged with armed robbery in McLean County Memorial Day parades, ceremonies planned in Central Illinois Normal police: 1 arrested after Thursday shooting on Shelbourne Carius: Remembering the site that housed many Bloomington restaurants, including Chevys Fresh-Mex Looking for something to do this weekend in Central Illinois? Here's the list. American Giants Museum bringing new statues to Atlanta upon first anniversary Miller Park Zoo to relocate female snow leopard, 'Shree' Bloomington man detained on attempted murder charge in May 7 shooting Funerals pending for May 25 Flick: When a job becomes a passion 1 injured in Shelbourne shooting; Normal police continue to investigate\n\nSHR this year fields Cup cars for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. Berry and Gragson are in their first seasons with the team. SHR holds the 2025 option on Briscoe and he has not been permitted to discuss future employment options even as rumors have swirled that SHR would close.\n\n\"Stewart Haas has been home to my family and I for the last 7 years and at the end of the year myself and the entire organization will be looking for a new home and new opportunities in the Cup series,\" Briscoe posted on social media. \"I have amazing partners behind me and can't wait to get them back in victory lane.\"\n\nThe move will also shutter the SHR Xfinity Series team, whose two cars are driven by Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nGene Haas founded Haas CNC Racing in 2002 and the California businessman lured Stewart in as a co-owner ahead of the 2009 season. Stewart had won two Cup championships for Joe Gibbs Racing at the time but couldn't turn down an equity stake and opportunity to help a small team contend for titles.\n\nStewart in his 2009 debut season gave the rebranded team its first Cup victory -- he won four races that year -- and its first Cup title in 2011. Kevin Harvick added a second championship in 2014.\n\nStewart, Harvick and Clint Bowyer have all retired from NASCAR driving and SHR since then has been in a grueling rebuild. The organization's last Cup Series win was in 2022 with Harvick a year before he retired. SHR didn't win a Cup race last season.\n\nThe team also is set to lose some of its support from Ford at the end of the season, although Mark Rushbrook, the global director of Ford Performance, told The Associated Press last week he had no idea what SHR's plans are beyond this year.\n\nSHR also lost major sponsorship this season when Smithfield Foods exited NASCAR and Anheuser-Busch moved to Trackhouse Racing.\n\nListen now and subscribe: Apple Podcasts | Google Podcasts | Spotify | RSS Feed | SoundStack | All Of Our Podcasts\n\nHaas spends most of his time with his Formula 1 team and Stewart is driving a full NHRA schedule, making both absentee owners at NASCAR events. The 71-year-old Haas was also ill for much of last year.\n\nThe NASCAR team is primarily run by Joe Custer, the chief operating officer and longtime Gene Haas confidant. His son, Cole, won the Xfinity championship last year for SHR.\n\nAmong SHR's accomplishments are the two Cup titles, two Xfinity championships and victories that include crown-jewel events such as the Daytona 500, Brickyard 400 and Southern 500.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said. \"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nPart of Haas' F1 team is run from the Kannapolis-based shop and it is unclear if that will continue or if Haas has plans to also depart from F1.\n\nIt's also not clear what happens to the four charters SHR holds that guarantee entry into the field every week. Spire Motorsports last year bought a charter for $40 million, but the actual charter value fluctuates annually.\n\nTeams are in a bitter fight with NASCAR over charters, which are set to expire at the end of this season. The teams want them made permanent and not renewable but NASCAR has refused to budge on the issue.\n\nShould SHR be able to sell the charters, it appears there is interest from Front Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing and Trackhouse. There is also speculation that Joe Custer may retain one of the charters and run a car for his son.\n\nWhere SHR's drivers land is unknown. Briscoe should be able to start talking to other teams now about his future. The team also held an option for next year on Berry, who doesn't bring much personal sponsorship and got the break of his career when SHR hired him ahead of this season.\n\nGragson's contract was announced as a multi-year deal and has backing from Bass Pro Shops to take to another team. Preece is in a contract year with SHR so was already free to shop around the series.\n\nCole Custer could end up in a car in either Cup or the Xfinity Series with backing of Haas' CNC Automation company, wile Herbst has significant financial backing from Monster Energy that should give him options.\n\nAP auto racing: https://apnews.com/hub/auto-racing\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. {"uri": "8150534493", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "21:34:25", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T21:34:25Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T21:33:52Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7843137383460999, "url": "https://www.forbes.com/sites/josephwolkin/2024/05/28/stewart-haas-racing-announces-closure-of-nascar-cup-series-team/", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing Announces Closure Of Nascar Cup Series Team", "body": "Tony Stewart and Gene Haas have announced plans to sell their four Nascar Cup Series charters and shut down their four-car team at the end of the 2024 season. Stewart-Haas Racing, which won the 2011 championship with Stewart and the 2014 title with Kevin Harvick, did not say what teams are in discussions to purchase the charters.\n\n\"We have made the difficult decision to close Stewart-Haas Racing at the conclusion of the 2024 season,\" a joint statement from Stewart and Haas said. \"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly.\n\n\"The commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nThe decision by SHR comes after Harvick and Aric Almirola retired, which coincided with the loss of major partners, such as Anheuser-Busch, Smithfield and Hunt Brothers Pizza. The team added Noah Gragson and Josh Berry to its driver lineup this season, with Bass Pro Shops picking up significant inventory on Gragson's car and Overstock.com doing so with Berry.\n\nThere are numerous landing spots for SHR's charters, including Trackhouse Racing, Front Row Motorsports and 23XI Racing, each of which are looking to expand to three full-time entries in 2025. The going rate for the charters will likely be around the $20 to 30 million range based on the high supply rate.\n\nTrackhouse has Ross Chastain and Daniel Suarez under contract, along with Zane Smith and Shane van Gisbergen. Front Row is losing Michael McDowell at the end of the season, but if it purchases another charter, it could absorb part of SHR's Cup operation and its employees. 23XI can either pick up a free agent driver, or it may elevate top Toyota prospect Corey Heim.\n\nSHR has not won a Cup Series race since Harvick's final victory at Richmond in 2022. While the team has begun to show improvements in its performance, it is rumored that they are no longer one of Ford's primary teams. Last year, Harvick was the only SHR driver to qualify for the playoffs compared to 2020, when all four cars made the playoffs.\n\nSHR formed in 2009 after Stewart announce he would depart Joe Gibbs Racing to co-own what was previously known as Haas CNC Racing, which Haas operated.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies,\" the statement continued. \"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix.\n\n\"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nThe team has 69 Cup wins since it was formed, along with 22 Xfinity Series victories. SHR also won the 2023 Xfinity Series championship with Cole Custer, son of team president Joe Custer.\n\nStewart will continue to own a NHRA team, while Haas will focus on his Formula 1 operation.", (AP) - Stewart-Haas Racing will close its NASCAR teams at the end of this season.\n\nCo-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced the decision Tuesday after nearly a year of rumors that their four-car Cup Series team was looking to sell its charters and either scale back or exit the stock car series completely.\n\n\"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly,\" the owners said. \"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It\u00b4s part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we\u00b4ve reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it\u00b4s time to pass the torch.\"\n\nSHR this year fields Cup Series cars for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. Berry and Gragson are in their first seasons with the team. SHR holds the 2025 option on Briscoe and he has not been contractually permitted to discuss future employment options even as rumors have swirled that SHR would close.\n\nThe move will also shutter the SHR Xfinity Series team, with two cars driven by Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nGene Haas founded Haas CNC Racing in 2002 and the California businessman lured Stewart in as a co-owner ahead of the 2009 season. Stewart had won two Cup championships for Joe Gibbs Racing at the time but couldn't turn down an equity stake and opportunity to help a small team win races and contend for titles.\n\nFILE - NASCAR driver Tony Stewart announces he will become a driver and co-owner of Haas CNC Raging Thursday, July 10, 2008, at ChicagoLand Speedway in Joliet, Ill. Stewart-Haas Racing will close its NASCAR team at the end of the 2024 season, co-team owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas said in a joint statement Tuesday, May 28, 2024. (AP Photo/Nam Y. Huh, FIle)\n\nStewart in his 2009 debut season gave the rebranded team its first Cup victory - he won four races that year - and its first Cup title in 2011. Kevin Harvick added a second championship in 2014.\n\nStewart, Harvick and Clint Bowyer have all retired from NASCAR driving and SHR since then has been in a grueling rebuild.\n\nHaas spends most of his time these days with his Formula 1 team and Stewart is driving a full NHRA schedule, making both absentee owners at NASCAR events. Haas was also ill for much of last year.\n\nThe NASCAR team is primarily run by Joe Custer, the chief operating officer and longtime Gene Haas confidant. Son Cole won the Xfinity championship last year for SHR.\n\nAmong SHR's accomplishments are the two Cup titles, two Xfinity championships and more than 100 NASCAR races that include crown-jewel events such as the Daytona 500, Brickyard 400 and Southern 500.\n\n\"We\u00b4re proud of all the wins and championships we\u00b4ve earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said. \"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nPart of Haas' F1 team is run from the Kannapolis-based shop and it is unclear if that will continue or if Haas has plans to also depart from F1.\n\nAP Auto Racing: https://apnews.com/hub/auto-racing\n\nFILE - Team co-owner Carl Haas and Tony Stewart, right, pose with the NASCAR Sprint Cup Series season-championship trophy at Homestead-Miami Speedway in Homestead, Fla., Sunday, Nov. 20, 2011. {"uri": "8150483861", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "20:42:20", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T20:42:20Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T20:41:38Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7372549176216125, "url": "https://sports.yahoo.com/nascar-stewart-haas-racing-shutting-down-cup-series-team-at-end-of-2024-season-203904859.html", "title": "NASCAR: Stewart-Haas Racing shutting down Cup Series team at end of 2024 season", "body": "One of NASCAR's biggest teams is ceasing its Cup Series operations.\n\nStewart-Haas Racing announced Tuesday that it is shutting down its top-level NASCAR team. The team, formed in 2009 when Tony Stewart became a co-owner with Gene Haas, currently fields four cars in the Cup Series for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece.\n\nSHR's closure comes as the team lost two longtime sponsors at the end of the 2023 season. Busch Light moved to Ross Chastain's No. 1 car at Trackhouse Racing following Kevin Harvick's retirement and Smithfield left NASCAR completely when Aric Almirola retired from full-time competition.\n\nStewart became the first driver-owner to win a NASCAR Cup Series title when he won his third championship driving for SHR in 2011. Three years later, Harvick won the Cup Series title.\n\nSince then, things have slowly trended downwards for the team even as Harvick was a stalwart. Harvick was 13th in the points standings a season ago while Almirola, Briscoe and Preece all finished outside the top 20. The organization went winless across an entire Cup Series season for the first time ever.\n\nRumors of a downsizing or total shuttering have been floated for months as SHR did not have a contract with Ford beyond the 2024 season. Teams typically have their manufacturers lined up years into the future.\n\nThe closure of Stewart-Haas means that teams looking to expand may not have to pay top rate for a charter -- essentially NASCAR's version of a franchise. The 36 cars with charters are guaranteed entry into every single Cup Series race and also a bigger share of prize money.\n\nThe only charter on the market ahead of the 2024 season sold for approximately $40 million when Spire purchased Live Fast Racing's charter in September of 2023. With all four SHR charters now on the market, it'll be a surprise if any of the team's guaranteed entries sell for close to that number.\n\nTrackhouse could be in the market for another charter along with Front Row Motorsports. Trackhouse is loaning Zane Smith to Spire Motorsports in 2024 and an additional charter or two can make room at the two-car team for him and/or Shane van Gisbergen.\n\nThe charter agreement between NASCAR and teams currently limits teams to a maximum of four charters. However, that agreement expires at the end of the 2024 season and the sanctioning body and its teams don't seem close to terms on a new deal. {"uri": "8150480329", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "20:38:40", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T20:38:40Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T20:38:15Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.729411780834198, "url": "https://sports.yahoo.com/stewart-haas-racing-close-operation-163053466.html", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to close operation at end of 2024 season", "body": "Stewart-Haas Racing will close its NASCAR operation at the conclusion of the 2024 season, co-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced Tuesday.\n\n\"We have made the difficult decision to close Stewart-Haas Racing at the conclusion of the 2024 season. It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly.\n\n\"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding.\n\n\"But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause -- winning races and collecting trophies.\n\n\"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix.\n\n\"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nStewart-Haas Racing's four-car Cup team currently fields the Nos. 4, 10, 14 and 41 Fords for drivers Josh Berry, Noah Gragson, Chase Briscoe and Ryan Preece, respectively. Two Xfinity Series teams also carry the SHR banner (Cole Custer, Riley Herbst).\n\nHaas has fielded Cup Series entries each season since 2002, originally under the banner of Haas CNC Racing. In 2008, eventual NASCAR Hall of Famer Stewart joined forces with Haas to form SHR for its inaugural season in 2009, starting with a two-car outfit with drivers Stewart and 2008 Daytona 500 winner Ryan Newman with a technical alliance with Hendrick Motorsports.\n\nMORE: Cup standings\n\nStewart scored the program's first victory in the 2009 NASCAR All-Star Race exhibition, then went to Victory Lane at Pocono Raceway to net the team's first points-paying victory three weeks later. Stewart ultimately scored four wins in the team's inaugural campaign in the No. 14 Chevrolet.\n\nTheir success continued in 2011, when Stewart and outgoing crew chief Darian Grubb won five of the 10 races in the NASCAR Playoffs -- including the season finale -- to claim Stewart-Haas Racing's first NASCAR Cup Series championship, edging Roush Fenway Racing's Carl Edwards (a Class of 2025 NASCAR Hall of Fame inductee) for the title in a tiebreaker.\n\nStewart-Haas Racing expanded to a three-car team for the 2013 season with Danica Patrick in the No. 10 car before adding a fourth car in 2014. Kevin Harvick shifted from Richard Childress Racing to SHR's renumbered No. 4 car with crew chief Rodney Childers after Ryan Newman's departure from the No. 39, and 2004 champion Kurt Busch, who slotted into the team's new No. 41 car.\n\nIn their first year together, Harvick and Childers rocketed to a five-win campaign that resulted in a Cup championship. The pairing lasted a decade, culminating in 37 of Harvick's 60 career wins before his retirement after the 2023 season.\n\nBusch added a milestone win to his resume -- as well as Stewart's -- by winning the 2017 Daytona 500 with crew chief Tony Gibson atop the pit box. Stewart never won the \"Great American Race\" as a driver but celebrated the triumph as a team co-owner in his first season after his Cup driving retirement.\n\nAdditional drivers through SHR's Cup tenure included Clint Bowyer, Aric Almirola, Daniel Su\u00e1rez and Cole Custer.\n\nWhile Stewart-Haas hasn't won since August 2022, when Harvick scored consecutive victories at Michigan International {"uri": "8150534546", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "21:34:40", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T21:34:40Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T21:33:56Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7254902124404907, "url": "https://heraldcourier.com/news/state-and-regional/stewart-haas-racing-to-close-nascar-teams-at-end-of-2024-season-says-time-to/article_6920a00a-94ba-582e-8fa0-8f5733e1b820.html", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to close NASCAR teams at end of 2024 season, says time to 'pass the torch'", "body": "By JENNA FRYER - AP Auto Racing Writer\n\nCHARLOTTE, N.C. (AP) -- Stewart-Haas Racing, a two-time NASCAR championship team with 69 Cup Series victories since its 2009 formation, will close its organization at the end of this season\n\nCo-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced the decision after nearly a year of rumors that their four-car Cup team was looking to sell its charters and either scale back or exit the stock car series completely. The news was delivered to the nearly 300 SHR employees late Tuesday afternoon.\n\n\"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly,\" the owners said. \"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nPeople are also reading... PREP FOOTBALL: Former Abingdon QB Jake Hess is the new head coach at John Battle after four seasons as assistant VHSL Regional Baseball, Softball, Soccer Preview Capsules for Thursday's Games VHSL Regional Preview Capsules for Friday's Baseball and Softball Games PREP BASEBALL: Chance Parker scores Lebanon's only run as Pioneers edge Union in pitching duel between Barton, Neff REGION 3D BASEBALL: Abingdon earns walk-off quarterfinal win over Hidden Valley VHSL PLAYOFF PRIMER: Hogoheegee (baseball, soccer) and Cumberland (softball) well-represented as Region 1D tourneys resume today Abingdon and Saltville lead charge in electric vehicle movement Man arrested after driving vehicle with deceased female in rear seat REGION 1D BASEBALL: Patrick Henry hammers out hits in 14-5 road win over Eastside Opinions vary on proposed solar program in Washington TUESDAY'S PREP ROUNDUP: Eastside wins Cumberland District baseball tourney; Rye Cove (baseball) earns Region 1D tourney bid; Tennessee High girls tennis falls at state; Abingdon boys, girls tennis in region finals; Jack Clem (Richlands) wins tennis gold New play shines a spotlight on the legendary woman's journey in 'Grandma Gatewood Took a Walk' Floyd, Christiansburg students face mob charges 2024 GENE \"PAPPY\" THOMPSON FINALIST NO. 1: Taylor Clay, Eastside SATURDAY'S PREP ROUNDUP: John Battle (boys) and Marion (girls) join Abingdon and George Wythe (girls) as recently crowned region tennis champs\n\nSHR this year fields Cup cars for Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. Berry and Gragson are in their first seasons with the team. SHR holds the 2025 option on Briscoe and he has not been permitted to discuss future employment options even as rumors have swirled that SHR would close.\n\n\"Stewart Haas has been home to my family and I for the last 7 years and at the end of the year myself and the entire organization will be looking for a new home and new opportunities in the Cup series,\" Briscoe posted on social media. \"I have amazing partners behind me and can't wait to get them back in victory lane.\"\n\nThe move will also shutter the SHR Xfinity Series team, whose two cars are driven by Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nGene Haas founded Haas CNC Racing in 2002 and the California businessman lured Stewart in as a co-owner ahead of the 2009 season. Stewart had won two Cup championships for Joe Gibbs Racing at the time but couldn't turn down an equity stake and opportunity to help a small team contend for titles.\n\nStewart in his 2009 debut season gave the rebranded team its first Cup victory -- he won four races that year -- and its first Cup title in 2011. Kevin Harvick added a second championship in 2014.\n\nStewart, Harvick and Clint Bowyer have all retired from NASCAR driving and SHR since then has been in a grueling rebuild. The organization's last Cup Series win was in 2022 with Harvick a year before he retired. SHR didn't win a Cup race last season.\n\nThe team also is set to lose some of its support from Ford at the end of the season, although Mark Rushbrook, the global director of Ford Performance, told The Associated Press last week he had no idea what SHR's plans are beyond this year.\n\nSHR also lost major sponsorship this season when Smithfield Foods exited NASCAR and Anheuser-Busch moved to Trackhouse Racing.\n\nHaas spends most of his time with his Formula 1 team and Stewart is driving a full NHRA schedule, making both absentee owners at NASCAR events. The 71-year-old Haas was also ill for much of last year.\n\nThe NASCAR team is primarily run by Joe Custer, the chief operating officer and longtime Gene Haas confidant. His son, Cole, won the Xfinity championship last year for SHR.\n\nAmong SHR's accomplishments are the two Cup titles, two Xfinity championships and victories that include crown-jewel events such as the Daytona 500, Brickyard 400 and Southern 500.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said. \"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nPart of Haas' F1 team is run from the Kannapolis-based shop and it is unclear if that will continue or if Haas has plans to also depart from F1.\n\nIt's also not clear what happens to the four charters SHR holds that guarantee entry into the field every week. Spire Motorsports last year bought a charter for $40 million, but the actual charter value fluctuates annually.\n\nTeams are in a bitter fight with NASCAR over charters, which are set to expire at the end of this season. The teams want them made permanent and not renewable but NASCAR has refused to budge on the issue.\n\nShould SHR be able to sell the charters, it appears there is interest from Front Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing and Trackhouse. There is also speculation that Joe Custer may retain one of the charters and run a car for his son.\n\nWhere SHR's drivers land is unknown. Briscoe should be able to start talking to other teams now about his future. The team also held an option for next year on Berry, who doesn't bring much personal sponsorship and got the break of his career when SHR hired him ahead of this season.\n\nGragson's contract was announced as a multi-year deal and has backing from Bass Pro Shops to take to another team. Preece is in a contract year with SHR so was already free to shop around the series.\n\nCole Custer could end up in a car in either Cup or the Xfinity Series with backing of Haas' CNC Automation company, wile Herbst has significant financial backing from Monster Energy that should give him options.\n\nAP auto racing: https://apnews.com/hub/auto-racing\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. {"uri": "8150475149", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "20:33:51", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T20:33:51Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T20:33:09Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7058823704719543, "url": "https://www.foxsports.com/stories/nascar/stewart-haas-racing-ceasing-cup-operations-after-2024-selling-four-charters", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing ceasing Cup operations after 2024, selling four charters", "body": "Stewart-Haas Racing, which has won two Cup titles and captured 69 wins since its formation in 2009, will close after the 2024 season, shuttering a four-car Cup operation.\n\nCo-owners Gene Haas and Tony Stewart have appeared focused on other aspects of their businesses in recent years. Haas has a Formula 1 team that has struggled and the three-time Cup champion Stewart started an NHRA drag-racing team a couple of years ago that his wife drove for last year and Stewart is driving for this year.\n\nSHR has struggled in recent years and its hefty support from Ford is set to end after this season. It also lost two major sponsors in Smithfield and Anheuser-Busch prior to this year, so without that Ford support continuing it would have been difficult to sustain a four-car operation.\n\n\"We have made the difficult decision to close Stewart-Haas Racing at the conclusion of the 2024 season,\" Stewart and Haas said in a joint statement. \"It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly.\n\n\"Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding. But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\"\n\nThe organization has four charters that it can sell, and sources indicated at least three of them will go to existing Cup organizations -- one to Front Row Motorsports, one to 23XI Racing and one to Trackhouse Racing. All three of those organizations indicated they had no comment on any charter acquisitions today. Where the fourth charter goes is not clear.\n\nNot having SHR on the Cup grid will be eye-opening next season. SHR started with Haas operating Haas CNC Racing in 2002. Haas gave Stewart half the team in 2009 for him to come drive and help operate the organization. They won championships in 2011 with Stewart and 2014 with Kevin Harvick.\n\nThe organization has 69 Cup wins with the last coming in 2022 with Harvick, who retired after the 2023 season.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause -- winning races and collecting trophies,\" Stewart and Haas said in their statement.\n\n\"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix. We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nThe closure leaves Cup drivers Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson, Josh Berry and Ryan Preece in transition, as well as Xfinity Series drivers Cole Custer and Riley Herbst.\n\nHere's a quick look at what could happen with those drivers:\n\nBriscoe, who is 16th in the Cup standings, is the driver most often mentioned as a possibility to drive for Wood Brothers Racing next year with Harrison Burton on the hot seat as he struggles for the third consecutive year. Briscoe was in an option year with SHR and can now start to have more extensive talks with other teams.\n\nBerry, at 19th in the standings in his rookie season and who has surged over the last month, was under contract with SHR for next year but obviously is now looking for a ride. He doesn't have much personal sponsorship but now will be talking heavily to sponsors and teams. Whether he remains in Cup is still to be determined.\n\nGragson's impressive run in his first season at SHR as he sits 21st in the standings (he'd be 19th if not for a 35-point penalty earlier this year plus what appears to be support from Bass Pro Shops, potentially could give him Cup options either at Front Row Motorsports or other teams.\n\nPreece sits 28th in the standings (he'd be 22nd if not for a 35-point penalty earlier this year) was already looking for next year as his contract was up after this season. His future seems uncertain.\n\nCuster, the former Cup driver and defending Xfinity Series champion who is third in the Xfinity standings, will be driving a car next year but still to be determined whether it is Xfinity or Cup. SHR's Xfinity programs -- it not only fields two cars but also supplies cars to other Ford teams -- could be siphoned off into a new team. Also, if Haas wants to continue involvement in NASCAR, Custer would be the natural driver for his Haas Automation company to sponsor as it has sponsored Custer for several years and Custer's father, Joe, is an SHR executive who has worked on Haas motorsports programs for decades.\n\nHerbst, seventh in the Xfintiy standings, has sponsorship from Monster Energy, and that should give him options, potentially on the Cup side.\n\nFRM (which would have two seats available) and 23XI will be seeking drivers if they obtain charters and would need sponsorship as well for them, making them possible landing spots for Herbst.\n\nTrackhouse already has a logjam of drivers with Ross Chastain, Shane van Gisbergen and Zane Smith currently under contract and Daniel Suarez expecting to sign an extension soon. There is a possibility the new charter system could limit organizations to three charters, and if that happens, Trackhouse would have to form an alliance with another team, keep van Gisbergen in Xfinity next year or release one of its drivers.\n\nLegacy Motor Club, RFK Racing and JTG Daugherty Racing have all considered expansion but are not expected to be in play for any of the SHR charters. Dale Earnhardt Jr. confirmed to FOX Sports last week that JR Motorsports also is not part of those conversations.", "source": {"uri": "foxsports.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "FOX Sports"}, Then they evolved into rumors that Stewart-Haas Racing could shut down entirely.\n\nNow the Stewart and Gene Haas-owned organization, winners of the 2011 and 2014 Cup Series championships, have confirmed that they will indeed shut down at the end of the 2024 season.\n\nThe decision comes less than a year after the team wrapped up their first winless season since becoming Stewart-Haas Racing in 2009, when Stewart joined forces with Haas.\n\nThrough the first 14 races of the 2024 season, none of their four drivers or cars are above the playoff cut line, and none of them managed to race their way into the All-Star Race.\n\nThis is a team that led the series in wins with 12 in 2018 and 10 in 2020. They have 69 victories total, most recently Kevin Harvick's final victory at Richmond Raceway in August 2022.\n\nThe decision brings to the forefront two major questions. First, where do their four charters go? And second, where do the four drivers go?\n\nFront Row Motorsports, 23XI Racing, and Trackhouse Racing Team are said to be the frontrunners to acquire a Stewart-Haas Racing charter. Where the fourth one ends up remains to be seen. Regardless, four charters becoming available at once should effectively reset the charter market, to an extent, after years and years of skyrocketing prices.\n\nAs for the drivers, Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson, and Ryan Preece are now looking for new rides. Berry and Gragson are both in their first year with Stewart-Haas Racing behind the wheel of the No. 4 Ford and No. 10 Ford, respectively. Briscoe is in his fourth season behind the wheel of the No. 14 Ford, and Preece is in his second season behind the wheel of the No. 41 Ford.\n\nWith Stewart-Haas Racing no longer competing in the NASCAR Cup Series after the 2024 season, that leaves only two four-car teams: Hendrick Motorsports and Joe Gibbs Racing. {"uri": "8150478117", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "20:36:50", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T20:36:50Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T20:36:13Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6666666865348816, "url": "https://www.nytimes.com/athletic/5524487/2024/05/28/stewart-haas-racing-nascar-shut-down/", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to shut down at end of season", "body": "Stewart-Haas Racing, a two-time championship NASCAR Cup Series team that not long ago was regarded as a powerhouse within the sport, will cease operations at the end of the 2024 season.\n\nTeam co-owners Tony Stewart and Gene Haas announced the decision Tuesday, though such a move has been widely anticipated for weeks. SHR's four charters, effectively NASCAR's version of franchise licenses, are to be sold off over the coming weeks and months. SHR's choice to either downsize or outright shut down is something the team has been moving toward for some time. Several other team owners have either already submitted bids or expressed interest in doing so, according to sources involved in the bidding process.\n\n\"The commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch,\" Stewart and Haas said in a joint statement. \"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause -- winning races and collecting trophies.\n\n\"That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix.\"\n\nSince its 2009 formation, SHR has won 69 Cup races and two championships (Stewart in 2011 and Kevin Harvick in 2014). Only Hendrick Motorsports (six titles) and Team Penske (three) have won more championships during this span.\n\nSHR has four Cup drivers under contract: Josh Berry, Chase Briscoe, Noah Gragson and Ryan Preece. The future for drivers, crew chiefs and other employees within the organization -- which also fields two lower-level Xfinity Series teams -- is unclear.\n\nBerry has a year left on his two-year contract, SHR has an option on Briscoe's contract that must be exercised by this summer, Preece's contract is out at the end of the season, while Gragson has recently indicated that a return to SHR is not certain.\n\nSHR's origins date back to 2003 when Haas, a California billionaire, began fielding a Cup team on a part-time basis before eventually taking that team full-time in 2003.\n\nFrustrated by the lack of high-level success and wanting to break through and finally win, Haas enticed Stewart to leave the well-established Joe Gibbs Racing, where Stewart had won two championships, to join his fledgling team in 2009 by offering him an ownership stake in the team.\n\nWith Stewart's transformative ability behind the wheel, his star power off the track and his knowledge of how to build a championship-caliber organization, combined with Haas' business acumen and deep pocketbook, the renamed Stewart-Haas Racing quickly became a dominating force.\n\nStewart delivered four race victories in his first season. Then came a championship in 2011 that came in rollicking fashion with him winning five of 10 playoff races.\n\nIn addition to Stewart, SHR also signed several big stars during its initial years and touted a robust lineup of major sponsors. Most notably was Harvick, Stewart's good friend who joined in 2014 and brought Anheuser-Busch with him as his primary sponsor. That same year Harvick won SHR its second championship. And over the next several years he was a perennial title contender.\n\nThe 2020 season was SHR's last great campaign. Harvick won a series-best nine races and ran away with the regular-season points championship, but what appeared a surefire championship run ended with a surprising elimination in the semi-final playoff round.\n\nSHR has experienced a gradual decline since 2021. Its four Cup teams have combined to win just four races, including a winless 2023 season and, thus far, a winless 2024.\n\nMeanwhile, SHR's downfall coincides with increased criticism of Stewart and Haas that their involvement in the team has decreased. Both Stewart and Haas own teams in other motorsports series -- Stewart owns a multi-car NHRA team that he also drives for full-time, while Haas owns a Formula One team. That each seemingly focuses most of their attention on these ventures over SHR hasn't gone unnoticed.\n\nEven though the demise of SHR seemed to be coming for months, the downfall is difficult to grasp. Only four years ago, SHR won 10 races and saw all four drivers make the playoffs -- a quarter of the entire NASCAR Cup Series playoff field. The idea such a major team could go away seemed unthinkable at the time, but the decline has been swift and sudden.\n\nChampionship-winning teams don't typically disappear, although 2017 Cup winner Furniture Row Racing shut its doors after the previous financial model grew too unwieldy for team owner Barney Visser. But aside from that, every championship team in the 2000s still exists, which underscores how unusual this is. Teams that shut their doors are typically less-funded, smaller teams that find they can no longer compete in today's Cup Series. But a powerhouse four-car team -- one of just three remaining in Cup -- and funded by a billionaire? That just doesn't happen. -- Jeff Gluck, motorsports staff writer\n\nThere's nothing \"silly\" about people losing their jobs, but SHR's news has already set off a scramble within the industry to find positions at other teams. That includes drivers, crew chiefs, crew members and everyone in between, but the drivers will obviously get the bulk of the attention.\n\nWhat happens to Briscoe, who was viewed as the flagship driver after Harvick's departure? What about rookie Berry, who has barely gotten to show what he's capable of? Or Gragson, who has seemingly raced his way into a ride with a better-than-expected performance this season? Questions about Preece and the Xfinity Series drivers remain as well, and it will certainly be interesting to see where crew chief Rodney Childers lands (and if he'll be able to stay with his new driver Berry).\n\nEither way, it's an unfortunate and sad situation for an operation of roughly 300 people who will now have to figure out what their futures hold. -- Gluck", "source": {"uri": {"uri": "8150474661", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-05-28", "time": "20:33:55", "dateTime": "2024-05-28T20:33:55Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-05-28T20:32:49Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6470588445663452, "url": "https://www.motorsport.com/nascar-cup/news/stewart-haas-racing-shutting-down-2024-berry-gragson-briscoe-preece/10616995/?fbclid=IwZXh0bgNhZW0CMTEAAR2dd2EIjlxw992-p4_E8hg0lPg4U5MHEn9C4NkQbhPqElHRP5nFrWxBiD0_aem_AfUrwRkf5XmsqHUt-lX7K-nkyxsA1kXirH6gLv1B2LlNbyWBl8kcouFXAZSUaCH-JVwZEHCQhW-Hcsp1g8TYwLau", "title": "Stewart-Haas Racing to shut down NASCAR Cup Series operation", "body": "On Tuesday, team co-owners Gene Haas and Tony Stewart released a joint statement explaining their decision to shutter the organization after 15 years.\n\n\"We have made the difficult decision to close Stewart-Haas Racing at the conclusion of the 2024 season. It is a decision that did not come easily, nor was it made quickly. Racing is a labor-intensive, humbling sport. It requires unwavering commitment and vast resources, with a 365-day mindset to be better than everyone else. It's part of what makes success so rewarding.\n\n\"But the commitment needed to extract maximum performance while providing sustainability is incredibly demanding, and we've reached a point in our respective personal and business lives where it's time to pass the torch.\n\n\"We're proud of all the wins and championships we've earned since joining together in 2009, but even more special is the culture we built and the friendships we forged as we committed to a common cause - winning races and collecting trophies. That is the same commitment we made to our personnel, our partners and our fans coming into this year, and that commitment will remain through the season finale at Phoenix.\n\n\"We have tremendous respect and appreciation for all of our employees, and we will work diligently to assist them during this transition to find new opportunities beyond the 2024 race season.\"\n\nTuesday's statement made no mention of the four charters Hass and Stewart currently hold in the Cup Series.\n\nThe charters, created with the start of the 2016 season, guarantees a team entry in all 36 points-paying races each year and sets a minimum guaranteed payout for each race. The payouts can change based on where the team ranks in owner points.\n\nHowever, the current charter agreement expires at the conclusion of this year and there is yet no new deal. That means, in essence, there are no charters for SHR to sell until an agreement is reached.\n\nSince the charters were introduced, they have increased more than 10 times in value. Spire Motorsports purchased Live Fast Motorsports' charter reportedly for around $40 million last year.\n\nThere has been an air of uncertainty around SHR's future for some time.\n\nOnce a dominant force in the Cup Series, the team has failed to win a Cup race in nearly two years. When Kevin Harvick and Aric Almirola retired from full-time competition at the end of last year, major backers Busch Beer and Smithfield left as well.\n\nThe team entered 2024 with four young drivers and just one Cup win between them. Although they have shown slight overall improvement in comparison to last year, the team is still nowhere near where a four-car operation is expected to be.\n\nJoe Gibbs Racing and Hendrick Motorsports are the only other teams that possesses four charters. Both have won several races and hold seven of the top eight spots in the championship standings. The highest SHR driver is Chase Briscoe in 16th.\n\nThe news leaves unclear futures for Briscoe, as well as his team-mates Noah Gragson, Josh Berry, and Ryan Preece. There's also intrigue involving the future of SHR's veteran crew chiefs, especially Rodney Childers, who has scored 40 wins from atop the pit box, earning the bulk of SHR's victories with Harvick. Previously, he guided Michael Waltrip Racing to its first-ever win with David Reutimann in 2009, as well as its last victory with Brian Vickers in 2013.\n\nSHR has 69 wins at the Cup level and last visited Victory Lane with Harvick at Richmond Raceway in August 2022. Stewart delivered the team its first championship in 2011 while Harvick earned the team's second title in 2014.\n\nThe fall-off for SHR has been staggering. It won 26 races between 2018 and 2020, only to win a total of four in the three seasons that followed.\n\nIn 2020, all four SHR drivers made the playoffs. In 2023, three of their four teams missed the cut. Harvick was the only driver to make the 16-driver field last year but was eliminated after the first round.\n\nThe loss of the SHR organization would also leave a significant hole in Ford Performance's NASCAR Cup program.
